casual riders use Cyclistic bikes differently?\n","\n","In order to answer the question, the following steps are taken in order to prepare, process, analyze and share findings from the dataset and The top 10 stations, as listed above, are those that are routinely used by casual and annual members. Hence, these stations can be prime locations to target casual customers into converting them into annual subscribers. "]},{"cell_type":"markdown","id":"c362ae90","metadata":{"papermill":{"duration":0.342035,"end_time":"2024-05-10T07:29:40.296814","exception":false,"start_time":"2024-05-10T07:29:39.954779","status":"completed"},"tags":[]},"source":["## Conclusion:\n","### Key Takeaways:\n","* It appears that a significant portion of casual riders consist of those which use the service for leisure basis. These could be tourists or residents who only use the service to ride occasionally. \n","* Casual members use the service for 20 mins on average, with a high variance.\n","* Casual riders mainly ride on weekends and during peak evening hours and late hours. They are also mostly active during peak summer months. \n","* For annual riders, it appears they mainly use the service for their general daily commute, however many riders also use the service consistently on weekends as well.\n","* Annual members use the service for 12 mins on average, with a low variance, \n","* Annual members are also active year round consistently, except during the really cold winter months where usage drops significantly.\n","\n","### Recommendations:\n","The customers that need to be targeted include where there seems to be an overlap between annual members and casual riders. An effective marketing stategy would need to be developed to entice casual members to pay the annual fee. My recommendations include:\n","* Target casual customers with marketing campaigns in stations with large number of casual and annual riders.\n","* Target consistent weekend riders which are part of the casual base with attractive weekday promotions. \n","* Target casual customers in cold months as they will be most likely to use service in the summer months as well, \n","\n","In order to implement these recommendations, the next steps would involve:\n","* Build an effective way to differentiate between casual riders who use the service frequently versus tourists. This could include require mobile numbers or email addresses to get the bicycle and assigning a unique ID based on that number. \n","\n","Some further data that could be measured for further analysis:\n","* A unique user ID for all riders. For annual riders, this would be assigned when they sign up. For casual riders, it could be generated from their email address or phone number which can be required to sign up. This would help us to differentiate between frequent casual riders and tourists, as well as understand how much each annual member rides in a year.\n","* Weather data to analyze riding patterns by weather more effectively.\n","* Age, gender and occupation data for (consenting) annual members to understand our userbase.\n","* Pricing details for annual passes and casual (daily and hourly) passes to understand differences between pricing models.
